  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_57d655b6-43bb-46fa-9748-b9bbc76fb06d'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16605748772612769849"><b>Oprah Book Club® Selection, April 1997</b>: Members of the Church of Fire and Brimstone and God's Almighty Baptizing Wind spend their days and nights serving the Lord and waiting for the Rapture--that moment just before the Second Coming of Christ when the saved will be lifted bodily to heaven and the damned will be left behind to face the thousand years of tribulation on eart</span>
  <span id="freeText16605748772612769849" style="display:none"><b>Oprah Book Club® Selection, April 1997</b>: Members of the Church of Fire and Brimstone and God's Almighty Baptizing Wind spend their days and nights serving the Lord and waiting for the Rapture--that moment just before the Second Coming of Christ when the saved will be lifted bodily to heaven and the damned will be left behind to face the thousand years of tribulation on earth. The tribulation, according to Grandpa Herman, founder of Fire and Brimstone, will be an ugly time: "He said that we'd run out of food. That big bugs would chase us around and sting us with their tails . . . He said we'd turn on the faucet in the bathroom and find only blood running out . . . He said evil multitudes would come unto us and cut off our limbs, and that we wouldn't die . . . And then he'd say, 'But you don't have to be left behind. You can go straight to Heaven with all of God's special children if you'll only open your hearts to Jesus . . .'" <p> Such talk of damnation weighs heavy on the mind of Ninah Huff, the 15-year-old narrator of Sheri Reynolds's second novel, <i>The Rapture of Canaan</i>. To distract her from sinful thoughts about her prayer partner James, Ninah puts pecan shells in her shoes and nettles in her bed. But concentrating on the Passion of Jesus cannot, in the end, deter Ninah and James from their passion for each other, and the consequences prove both tragic and transforming for the entire community. </p><p> <i>The Rapture of Canaan</i> is a book about miracles, and in writing it, Reynolds has performed something of a miracle herself. Although the church's beliefs and practices may seem extreme (sleeping in an open grave, mortifying the flesh with barbed wire), its members are complex and profoundly sympathetic as they wrestle with the contradictions of Fire and Brimstone's theology, the temptations of the outside world, and the frailties of the human heart.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="16605748772612769849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1520943" />
    <a title="Sammy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/103544-sammy"><img alt="Sammy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264098311p2/103544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1520943?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sammy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sammy" href="/user/show/103544-sammy">Sammy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/103544-sammy?shelf=a-the-best">a-the-best</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1520943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5813451858049827992">First off, let me start by saying that this is not a religious book, it can be viewed that way if you want to, but in case you're one of those people that are scared off by religious books, this isn't one. Now, on to the more important matters...<br/><br/>Almost from the first word I had become sucked into this book and Ninah's character, a flawed, naive girl who truly doesn't know better. She's sweet, tries hard, but just doesn't know what she needs to know. The way Reynolds has written her, doesn't make</span>
  <span id="freeText5813451858049827992" style="display:none">First off, let me start by saying that this is not a religious book, it can be viewed that way if you want to, but in case you're one of those people that are scared off by religious books, this isn't one. Now, on to the more important matters...<br /><br />Almost from the first word I had become sucked into this book and Ninah's character, a flawed, naive girl who truly doesn't know better. She's sweet, tries hard, but just doesn't know what she needs to know. The way Reynolds has written her, doesn't make her naivity annoying, but just adds to her character.<br /><br />Part of what makes this book so interesting is that it's written in a way that completely immerses you in their obscure and different world, but allows you to keep your own knowledge and ideals about you, so that you look back and can still think, "That's so wrong!"<br /><br />Ninah goes through a trying journey and we are along for the ride. I was enthralled with every character that graced the pages of this book. Even though they may only show up in one sentence, Reynolds writes in such a way that you know if you asked her she could give a complete history about that character. This book holds so much depth to it, but it's presented in such a way that the reader doesn't feel like their drowning.<br /><br />The one small problem I did have was that the ending seemed a little too abrupt. Perhaps it's just me, but I felt there wasn't enough closure and I wanted to know a little more. But what I dislike, someone else may love.<br /><br />There's a lot more I want to say about the book, but I would end up giving too much away. This is definitely a book I say you should read. Beautiful, touching and moving every word pulls you even more into this world that the feeling of disgust you felt at the beginning has turned to pity, and in some weird way, a small glimmer of joy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5813451858049827992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_139064546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139064546" />
    <a title="Robert Pajer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2961278-robert-pajer"><img alt="Robert Pajer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442505895p2/2961278.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139064546?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert Pajer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert Pajer" href="/user/show/2961278-robert-pajer">Robert Pajer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139064546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer854977817722321156">Sheri Reynolds paints a vivid picture of "Bible Belt Cultism," as seen through the eyes of a teen-age girl named, Ninah. The Church of Fire and Brimstone and God's Almighty Baptizing Wind is pastored by Ninah's Grandfather, Herman Langston, who, as Ninah says, "Used the Bible, of course, but only the parts he liked. He had the habit of altering verses just a little to make them match his own beliefs." The church of about eighty members is composed mostly of Ninah's family and Reynolds, through N</span>
  <span id="freeText854977817722321156" style="display:none">Sheri Reynolds paints a vivid picture of "Bible Belt Cultism," as seen through the eyes of a teen-age girl named, Ninah. The Church of Fire and Brimstone and God's Almighty Baptizing Wind is pastored by Ninah's Grandfather, Herman Langston, who, as Ninah says, "Used the Bible, of course, but only the parts he liked. He had the habit of altering verses just a little to make them match his own beliefs." The church of about eighty members is composed mostly of Ninah's family and Reynolds, through Ninah, lets us view the constricted lives of the church members under the tyrannical rule of Grandpa Herman. <br /><br />Their loyalty to the dictatorial Grandfather is a sober reminder of the danger involved when charismatic individuals, manipulating the Scriptures, suppress the weak and shape their lives with false doctrines. The price is excessive for such manipulation and at the Church of Fire and Brimstone it is paid out in emotionally devastated lives. The characters are addictive, the narrative exquisite, and the plot captivating. Sheri Reynolds has written a powerful novel. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="854977817722321156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2761759?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie" href="/user/show/113160-annie">Annie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425155431" href="/book/show/1001966.Rapture_of_Canaan">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2761759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12135600078937883840">I just finished reading this book for the second time. I think I loved it more than the first. The only books I tend to give 5 stars to are books that make me want to reinvent my life when they are over, live a better life, and be a better person. This really isn't that kind of book but it is greatness through and through.<br/><br/>There were times while reading this book that I just needed to put it down. I knew if I kept reading I would get too sad. I was right there with Ninah, going through her strugg</span>
  <span id="freeText12135600078937883840" style="display:none">I just finished reading this book for the second time. I think I loved it more than the first. The only books I tend to give 5 stars to are books that make me want to reinvent my life when they are over, live a better life, and be a better person. This really isn't that kind of book but it is greatness through and through.<br /><br />There were times while reading this book that I just needed to put it down. I knew if I kept reading I would get too sad. I was right there with Ninah, going through her struggles. I wanted to so badly to reach in and tell her that everything would be okay, that she was doing just fine. I couldn't though. I had to sit back and watch her suffer and wait for James to tell her that she was "doing good". <br /><br />I don't want to be Ninah or have her life. I do aspire to have her strength to see through the twisted community that there is no escaping from. Like all of us, her life is what it is. She will forever be influenced by it but she has discovered that she can form her own opinions, make her own choices, and she is her own person. It is a lesson that we all need to learn.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12135600078937883840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1302152132" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1302152132" />
    <a title="Tracy Sherman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7917746-tracy-sherman"><img alt="Tracy Sherman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330230016p2/7917746.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1302152132?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy Sherman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy Sherman" href="/user/show/7917746-tracy-sherman">Tracy Sherman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1302152132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1843905463435948269">I started this book with just one expectation, that I wasn't going to like it. I just finished a coming of age story set in the south that started off so promising and ended cliché and disappointing. In the beginning of this book it seemed like I'd be in for the same experience. Then about 20 to 30% into the book I found myself very engaged. <br/>The young protagonist has a very real voice, her grandmother and grandfather, the other leading characters of the book are also very interesting and well wr</span>
  <span id="freeText1843905463435948269" style="display:none">I started this book with just one expectation, that I wasn't going to like it. I just finished a coming of age story set in the south that started off so promising and ended cliché and disappointing. In the beginning of this book it seemed like I'd be in for the same experience. Then about 20 to 30% into the book I found myself very engaged. <br />The young protagonist has a very real voice, her grandmother and grandfather, the other leading characters of the book are also very interesting and well written. <br />The grandfather runs a fire and brimstone Christian sect called, appropriately enough, "The Church of Fire and Brimstone and God’s Almighty Baptizing Wind." There's no particular mention made of last two words of the church's name so I guess nobody got the joke but me.<br />There's a pretty large congregation and everybody's related so at times it's difficult to realize who's being talked about and what their relationship is to everyone else, so it seems the auxiliary characters are all pretty much interchangeable. But when they move to a front position they are finely drawn, even if only for a paragraph or two. <br />The language, although sometimes adjective heavy never feels forced, and the situations although many times outrageous seem believable in the context of this religious sect. <br />And with what's going on in America about religious fundamentalism it makes this a very engrossing read. <br />I was going to give The Rapture of Canaan three stars but as the narrative progressed and engaged me I realized how good this book is. <br />Would I be remiss in saying it enraptured me? </span>
  <a data-text-id="1843905463435948269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6301807?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiffany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiffany" href="/user/show/337296-tiffany">Tiffany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">oprah's book club fans, religious fanatics, women</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/337296-tiffany?shelf=oprahsbookclublist">oprahsbookclublist</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6301807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14606326956517199226">I actually liked this book a lot I would have liked it more but I wasn't so big on the ending. There was quite a few very interesting chapters in a vague disjointed kind of way. <br/><br/>It's the story of a young girl who finds herself in a bit of a position after she gets pregnant. She lives within a cultish community that is so far overboard they are fanatics lead by Ninah's grandfather who wasn't the same when he came back from war. <br/><br/>It's got both interesting little sides stories in it, as well as the </span>
  <span id="freeText14606326956517199226" style="display:none">I actually liked this book a lot I would have liked it more but I wasn't so big on the ending. There was quite a few very interesting chapters in a vague disjointed kind of way. <br /><br />It's the story of a young girl who finds herself in a bit of a position after she gets pregnant. She lives within a cultish community that is so far overboard they are fanatics lead by Ninah's grandfather who wasn't the same when he came back from war. <br /><br />It's got both interesting little sides stories in it, as well as the main story, and her future. <br /><br />The author did everything she could to shock you while trying to make Ninah feel like it was completely normal... but she almost did it to well. The story is past the unbelievable line into ridicules by the end. Which is a shame. <br /><br />There was one thing from the book though I've taken with me and deeply thought about upon completion of it. Being a girl who loves to read stories about revenge... I liked this part of the book best. <br /><br />"Grudges are bad things, Ninah," she said at last. "There's only so much room in one heart. You can fill it up with love or you can fill it with resentment. But every bit of resentment you hold takes space away from the love. And the resentment don't do no good noway, but look what love can do."</span>
  <a data-text-id="14606326956517199226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1540180182" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1540180182" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10196629-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453589393p2/10196629.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1540180182?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/10196629-beverly">Beverly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6648132-the-rapture-of-canaan">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10196629-beverly?shelf=november-book-count">november-book-count</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10196629-beverly?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540180182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4056551272808103253">This book was definitely different. The story is centered around the lives of the members of the Church of Fire and Brimstone and God's Almighty Baptizing Wind. It takes place in a community where everyone in that particular neighborhood is related in one way or another and they all belong to that particular "church sect", headed up by Grandpa Herman. Basically everyone is primarily preparing for the Rapture but, of course, people being people...some are going to occasionally slip up. Their puni</span>
  <span id="freeText4056551272808103253" style="display:none">This book was definitely different. The story is centered around the lives of the members of the Church of Fire and Brimstone and God's Almighty Baptizing Wind. It takes place in a community where everyone in that particular neighborhood is related in one way or another and they all belong to that particular "church sect", headed up by Grandpa Herman. Basically everyone is primarily preparing for the Rapture but, of course, people being people...some are going to occasionally slip up. Their punishments could be anything from sleeping in an open grave overnight to sleeping on barbed wire. The narrator is a 15 year old girl who is experiencing her first romantic feelings and where that all leads. I can't say this was a page turner for me but it was certainly a fascinating look at a way of thinking way out of my imagination. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4056551272808103253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/918446-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490821302p2/918446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15756250?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie" href="/user/show/918446-stephanie">Stephanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer15756250&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15756250" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17402897358964897455">Good. Mixes fundamentalist elements of <i>The Chrysalids</i> with sacred/bloody imagery of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6149.Beloved' title='Beloved by Toni Morrison' rel='nofollow noopener'>Toni Morrison</a>’s <i>Beloved</i>. A little strange because of certain images of Jesus that are morphed into sexually charged adolescent dreams.<br/>	<br/><b>Summary</b><br/>Ninah grows up in a community of extended family that centers around a fundamentalist church led by her Grandpa Herman. After her “prayer partner” James learns that she is carrying his baby he drowns himself rather than face Herman’s cruel punishments. <br/>Ninah is nearly cast </span>
  <span id="freeText17402897358964897455" style="display:none">Good. Mixes fundamentalist elements of <i>The Chrysalids</i> with sacred/bloody imagery of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6149.Beloved" title="Beloved by Toni Morrison" rel="nofollow noopener">Toni Morrison</a>’s <i>Beloved</i>. A little strange because of certain images of Jesus that are morphed into sexually charged adolescent dreams.<br />	<br /><b>Summary</b><br />Ninah grows up in a community of extended family that centers around a fundamentalist church led by her Grandpa Herman. After her “prayer partner” James learns that she is carrying his baby he drowns himself rather than face Herman’s cruel punishments. <br />Ninah is nearly cast out when the community learns she is pregnant out of wedlock. She claims the child is holy, born of God, and is “dunked” for her blasphemy in the same pond James drowned in. During her pregnancy she is placed in isolation where her only consolation is her “Nanna” who speaks frankly about both her distaste for Herman’s law and her uncompromising love for her husband. <br /><br />When Canaan is born, the community is shocked to see the “sign” of his hands, which are permanently joined in prayer. As the new “mother of God”, Ninah enjoys new freedoms, like cutting her hair and wearing James’s clothes. However, Canaan is given over to another couple who could not have children and who restrict Ninah’s corrupting visits.<br />	<br />Herman has a stroke. Nanna cares for him, though he rarely recognizes her as his wife. He wanders away one day and the community thinks he has been raptured; they’ve been left behind. Then he returns. <br />	<br />Ninah steals away with Canaan as the community erupts in confusion. Story ends with Ninah cutting Canaan’s palms apart, praising his normality. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17402897358964897455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_228175868" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228175868" />
    <a title="Ibis3" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4093912-ibis3"><img alt="Ibis3" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280687218p2/4093912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228175868?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ibis3" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ibis3" href="/user/show/4093912-ibis3">Ibis3</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093912-ibis3?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093912-ibis3?shelf=united-states">united-states</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093912-ibis3?shelf=religion">religion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093912-ibis3?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093912-ibis3?shelf=free">free</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093912-ibis3?shelf=2005">2005</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093912-ibis3?shelf=women">women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093912-ibis3?shelf=twentieth-century">twentieth-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228175868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8560875019319685105">My original review (24-3-05):<br/><br/>'I had some major difficulties with the book though, for example: the narrator is supposed to be Ninah, but her voice as narrator (poetical, adult & educated) is completely different from her voice as a speaking character (dialectical: e.g. "ain't", "don't reckon", double negatives); in a related way, Ninah's almost uncanny insights seem too externally derived. I just can't see a 12-15 year old girl who lives in such an insular community having such an ability to be </span>
  <span id="freeText8560875019319685105" style="display:none">My original review (24-3-05):<br /><br />'I had some major difficulties with the book though, for example: the narrator is supposed to be Ninah, but her voice as narrator (poetical, adult &amp; educated) is completely different from her voice as a speaking character (dialectical: e.g. "ain't", "don't reckon", double negatives); in a related way, Ninah's almost uncanny insights seem too externally derived. I just can't see a 12-15 year old girl who lives in such an insular community having such an ability to be so objective about what she's been taught (even if what Leila says and what she experiences in school give her extra knowledge or ideas). Also, James' motivation was never really made clear. I'm sure that what he did would have been considered an ultimate sin, even worse than fornication. Wouldn't he have been more afraid of the consequences for that? I guess one could put it down to teenage confusion, not helped by having to sleep on a bed of thorns, or the knowledge of what they did to Ben.<br /><br />The strange mixture of sincere belief and hypocrisy of all the characters made the story intriguing, but at the same time made me a little sceptical. I found the writing to be a bit self-consciously pretentious at times (especially the opening &amp; closing paragraphs which could have been edited out).<br /><br />However, all that said, it was fairly well written, the characters (especially Ninah and James) were well developed, and the plot &amp; setting fascinating. There were parts of it I really enjoyed &amp; it left me wondering what would happen next.'</span>
  <a data-text-id="8560875019319685105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_206204082" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206204082" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/981388-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1290055198p2/981388.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206204082?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/981388-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206204082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2043185347486692540">I think I give everything three stars. I think the star rating system is messed up. But, that's a soapbox discussion for another day. I enjoyed The Rapture of Canaan. Reynolds writing is top notch. It is however, very Oprah book club-- well written, well drawn characters, who go through a whole lot of crud. The good thing is the crud moves along quickly in this one. I didn't feel like I was bogged down forever, and looked forward to opportunities to read. On the flip side, I wish Reynolds would </span>
  <span id="freeText2043185347486692540" style="display:none">I think I give everything three stars. I think the star rating system is messed up. But, that's a soapbox discussion for another day. I enjoyed The Rapture of Canaan. Reynolds writing is top notch. It is however, very Oprah book club-- well written, well drawn characters, who go through a whole lot of crud. The good thing is the crud moves along quickly in this one. I didn't feel like I was bogged down forever, and looked forward to opportunities to read. On the flip side, I wish Reynolds would have fleshed things out a bit. I understand the main character is meant to be seen as brainwashed and naive, and that's ok, but she seems to remain naive, despite her transformation. Also, the surrounding characters seem thin. So, overall I enjoyed it, but found it lacking somehow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2043185347486692540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1307464317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1307464317" />
    <a title="Daniel Simmons" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5904365-daniel-simmons"><img alt="Daniel Simmons" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311864474p2/5904365.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1307464317?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Simmons" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Simmons" href="/user/show/5904365-daniel-simmons">Daniel Simmons</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1307464317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6231551962568384434">After a middling beginning (wait, is that an etymological contradiction?), this book picked up steam, then lost some steam, then became downright steamy, then doused itself with cold lake water, then I give up on this metaphor. It was an easy read but seldom a very compelling one, partly because I found the antagonist (Grandpa Herman) unconvincing and that made the whole frame of his religious fringe community unconvincing as well. Overall: Not bad, but nothing special. Probably best suited for </span>
  <span id="freeText6231551962568384434" style="display:none">After a middling beginning (wait, is that an etymological contradiction?), this book picked up steam, then lost some steam, then became downright steamy, then doused itself with cold lake water, then I give up on this metaphor. It was an easy read but seldom a very compelling one, partly because I found the antagonist (Grandpa Herman) unconvincing and that made the whole frame of his religious fringe community unconvincing as well. Overall: Not bad, but nothing special. Probably best suited for YA female readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6231551962568384434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_420691181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420691181" />
    <a title="Laura Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8630626-laura-lee"><img alt="Laura Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333741874p2/8630626.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420691181?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Lee" href="/user/show/8630626-laura-lee">Laura Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420691181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11958856982149587365">One of the best books I have ever read! It was loving and heartbreaking and inspirational. Ninah was born into a community of holy rollers, with strict rules and regulations. As she falls in love, she begins to question the way things are done. I fell in love with Ninah and wanted her to come out whole. She's a wonderful, three dimensional character. I cried at the end, when she is finally released in her love. Beautifully written. I would highly recommend this book to anyone. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1287262939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1287262939" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/782103-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486806103p2/782103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1287262939?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/782103-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287262939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9910850899478608494">A fast read and (mostly) an engrossing one, although there are some melodramatic parts (weaving a cross? barbed wire? whut?). I was a bit sorry when Ninah fell in love, though; I could tell the rest of the story would be centred around that, and I found the beginning and its portrayal of the cult more interesting. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2700218277" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2700218277" />
    <a title="Steve Kreidler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1528302-steve-kreidler"><img alt="Steve Kreidler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362340804p2/1528302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2700218277?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve Kreidler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve Kreidler" href="/user/show/1528302-steve-kreidler">Steve Kreidler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2700218277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1609381741373421295">Amazing book in the General feel of classic southern gothic literature. Powerful writing. <br/><br/>Quote “When I’ve used up all my rugs and lies, rope and hair, fabric and love, when I’m out of twine and my loom is broken and there’s still a story in me, that’s when I unknot and begin the unraveling. My rugs are never finished. I use the same materials to make them over and over again, featuring something new each time and hearing a different tale. But sometimes they speak the most wisely when they are h</span>
  <span id="freeText1609381741373421295" style="display:none">Amazing book in the General feel of classic southern gothic literature. Powerful writing. <br /><br />Quote “When I’ve used up all my rugs and lies, rope and hair, fabric and love, when I’m out of twine and my loom is broken and there’s still a story in me, that’s when I unknot and begin the unraveling. My rugs are never finished. I use the same materials to make them over and over again, featuring something new each time and hearing a different tale. But sometimes they speak the most wisely when they are heaps of fibers on the pack house floor, intermingling and waiting. If I sit with them silent long enough, they will talk. Just listening, I can give them tongues. They will speak like prophets”.<br /><br />Ninah is a young girl moving toward adulthood who lives in a religious compound. Her questions about life and love and truth are universal. The religious setting provides context, but this is not a book about religious fervor. <br /><br />I highly recommend this and Reynolds’ other masterpiece, “A Gracious Plenty” to all my friends who revel in contemporary literature. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1609381741373421295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie Hoang-Pham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie Hoang-Pham" href="/user/show/55183345-annie-hoang-pham">Annie Hoang-Pham</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1933846163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14678081116387593637">(3.75) I LOVED the first half of the book. Then it started becoming too much. I felt like new elements kept getting added and added to the book to the point where I didn't want to pick up the book anymore. I thought the book could have been better if there were less crazy things going on and more of a focus on the bigger events. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gCMIgVPY7jRPbOonWLk4hw45d742knOz743jIRKfG0nrTBJmjYD2zGoEBhOOOPcrIR25T+cx0spWmQVWrzsRSA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+/PL+OdWZLkHh1L2JQYXnl08WSIOV1cQp463cygz68eQnNEfOQ58QSLvvsLzh9gychiX09/09mkemlEElZfhxg==')})
  }
//]]>

Sometimes it\'s hard to tell what to fear most—the fires and floods or the flesh-and-blood grifters, drunks, and busybodies who insinuate themselves into their new life. To survive, they must find out whether love can keep chaos and madness at bay. Their struggles with nature, with work, with the changing century, and with the disappointments and triumphs of their union make Gap Creek a timeless story of a marriage.\n\nA native of the North Carolina mountains, Robert Morgan was raised on land settled by his Welsh ancestors. An accomplished novelist and poet, he has won the James B. Hanes Poetry Prize, the North Carolina Award in Literature, and the Jacaranda Review Fiction Prize. His short stories have appeared in Prize Stories: The O. Henry Awards and New Stories from the South, and his novel The Truest Pleasure was a finalist for the Southern Book Critics Circle Award for Fiction.<\/span>\n  <a Yet returning to her hometown also brings her back to Hollis, March’s former soul mate and lover. March’s father had taken the teenaged Hollis, an abandoned child, and the product of a series of detention homes, into his house as a boarder, and treated him like a son. Yet March and Hollis’s passionate love was hardly a normal sibling relationship. When Hollis left her after a petty fight, March waited for him three long years, wondering what she had done wrong.\n\nEncountering Hollis again makes March acutely aware of the choices that she has made, and the choices everyone around her has made—including Mrs. Dale, who knew more of love than March could ever have suspected, and her brother Alan, whose tragic history has left him grief-struck, with alcohol as his only solace.           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10445464482063827198">Sheri Reynolds is an author of contemporary Southern fiction.<br/><br/>Sheri Reynolds was born and raised in rural South Carolina. She graduated from Conway High School in 1985, Davidson College in 1989, and Virginia Commonwealth University in 1992.<br/><br/>Her published novels include Bitterroot Landing, The Rapture of Canaan (an Oprah book club selection and New York Times bestseller), A Gracious Plenty (98), Fire</span>
  <span id="freeText10445464482063827198" style="display:none">Sheri Reynolds is an author of contemporary Southern fiction.<br /><br />Sheri Reynolds was born and raised in rural South Carolina. She graduated from Conway High School in 1985, Davidson College in 1989, and Virginia Commonwealth University in 1992.<br /><br />Her published novels include Bitterroot Landing, The Rapture of Canaan (an Oprah book club selection and New York Times bestseller), A Gracious Plenty (98), Firefly Cloak (06), The Sweet In-Between (08), and The Homespun Wisdom of Myrtle T. Cribb (12). Her first play, Orabelle's Wheelbarrow, won the Women Playwrights' Initiative playwriting competition for 2005. <br /><br />Also Professor of English and the Ruth and Perry Morgan Chair of Southern Literature at Old Dominion University in Norfolk, VA, Sheri teaches creative writing and literature classes. She won the Outstanding Faculty Award from the State Council for Higher Education of Virginia in 2003. In 2005, she received a grant from the Virginia Commission for the Arts in playwriting. She has also taught at Virginia Commonwealth University, The College of William and Mary, and Davidson College.<br /><br />Sheri lives in the town of Cape Charles on Virginia's Eastern Shore. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10445464482063827198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
